--- Commit Message ---
LU-11077 utils: mount with client-only params

Client-specific parameters can be added manually
to either '/etc/lustre/mount.client.params' or
'/etc/lustre/mount.FSNAME.params' to be set upon
the next client mount.

[ec2-user@ip-24-0-3-20 lustre-release]$ ldd lustre/utils/mount.lustre | wc -l
22

12

--- Message (Andreas Dilger, 2024-08-07 22:25:34.000000000) ---
Patch Set 37: Code-Review-1

(1 comment)

> Andreas, I wonder if the FSNAME is not enough here? It only looks
 > at the fs name on the export, but if somebody has two servers with
 > same fsname?

If someone has two different filesystems with the same FSNAME, then they are totally f****d for other reasons (e.g. all of the parameter names will conflict, probably many other Lustre commands will explode in strange and wonderful ways).  Don't Do That (tm)!
 
 > People love to give their fsname a very unique name "lustre" which
 > is also the default fsname I think? So if I have server1:/lustre
 > and server2:/lustre - suddenly there's no way to specify different
 > parameters for only one of them?

There *already* isn't a way to specify different parameters for those two filesystems.  Running "lctl set_param osc.lustre-*.max_dirty_mb" will already apply to both filesystems even without this change.


 > Of course it's a totally different matter that the server name
 > could be specified in a gazillion ways.  Should we juts thoroughly
 > document this so next time someboy gets surprised we just point them
 > at the documentation or is there something more sensible we can do?

No.  One gap with this patch is that there isn't any check to *force* that the parameters in mount.FSNAME.params are applied to only FSNAME.  It would _probably_ be reasonable, now that this is mentioned, to warn (or error?) if any parameter in mount.FSNAME.params does not itself contain FSNAME (simple strstr() check).  It is difficult to do the opposite and automatically add FSNAME to a parameter therein.  If someone *really* wants to have a global parameter in there then they could always edit the mount.FSNAME.params file, but I suspect this would never be needed.

--- Message (Oleg Drokin, 2024-08-07 22:36:47.000000000) ---
Patch Set 37:

> No.  One gap with this patch is that there isn't any check to *force* that the parameters in mount.FSNAME.params are applied to only FSNAME.  It would _probably_ be reasonable, now that this is mentioned, to warn (or error?) if any parameter in mount.FSNAME.params does not itself contain FSNAME (simple strstr() check).  It is difficult to do the opposite and automatically add FSNAME to a parameter therein.

Well, the check might not be so easy if the fsname is generic enough that it might match something already in the path (like lustre? hopefully nobody will call their filesystem osc, ldlm, mdt, and other such subsystems)

Also you would totally ruin clever people's hacks to set OTHER filesystems parameters when THIS one is mounted so this one gets priority or whatever. Though do they really need this much rope  and should we be the provider of it I don't know.

--- Message (Andreas Dilger, 2024-08-07 22:46:30.000000000) ---
Patch Set 37:

(3 comments)

> > No.  One gap with this patch is that there isn't any check to
 > *force* that the parameters in mount.FSNAME.params are applied to
 > only FSNAME.  It would _probably_ be reasonable, now that this is
 > mentioned, to warn (or error?) if any parameter in
 > mount.FSNAME.params does not itself contain FSNAME (simple strstr()
 > check).  It is difficult to do the opposite and automatically add
 > FSNAME to a parameter therein.
 > 
 > Well, the check might not be so easy if the fsname is generic
 > enough that it might match something already in the path (like
 > lustre? hopefully nobody will call their filesystem osc, ldlm, mdt,
 > and other such subsystems)

I think the FSNAME substring check can be specific enough by checking for some delimiter (e.g. '.', '-', '*') before and after the matched FSNAME string.  If the filesystem name is "osc" then they get what they deserve, and in the worst case it doesn't prevent them from shooting themselves in both feet, but it doesn't make the situation any worse.

 > Also you would totally ruin clever people's hacks to set OTHER
 > filesystems parameters when THIS one is mounted so this one gets
 > priority or whatever. Though do they really need this much rope 
 > and should we be the provider of it I don't know.

I've wanted this functionality for a long time, and I think there is a reasonable balance between "yes, there might be a few ways to get do wrong" and "people have already been doing it wrong for a long time and this is already better, and not worse".

--- Message (Andreas Dilger, 2024-08-07 23:19:30.000000000) ---
Patch Set 37: Code-Review+1

Sorry, I was thinking of the "LU-11077 utils: --client option for set_param" patch that is actually saving these parameters via "lctl set_param -C".  We can't do anything in this patch to stop the user foot-gun event, just like we already can't do that for "lctl set_param -P" and multiple client mounts.

--- Message (Andreas Dilger, 2024-08-23 00:53:34.000000000) ---
Patch Set 37:

> I am confused about the decision to statically link against
 > lustre_param.c rather than just linking against liblustre itself.
 > It doesn't seem any simpler. And from ldd, `mount.lustre` already
 > has something like 2x as many dynamic library dependencies
 > compared to `lctl`. What's one more?

Tim, the reason for this is a bit complex, and an artifact of how Lustre developer testing is done.  When running tests directly from the build tree (e.g. "make; cd lustre/tests; bash sanity.sh") we are still required to run the mount.lustre helper from /sbin when using "mount -t lustre ..." because that is the only place that mount will look for it (for security reasons if non-root users are able to trigger filesystem mounts).

In order for this one binary to be runnable from /sbin it is more complex to depend on a shared library that is also not installed in the system, so static linking of lustre_param.c was used to ensure mounting still worked in the various test environments (note 37 versions of this patch) and they could run "set_param" as needed.

To avoid dragging in a bunch of *other* files, a few stub functions were used to avoid dependencies for functionality that is not actually needed.  This shouldn't be needed elsewhere since most applications would link to liblustreapi.

--- Message (Andreas Dilger, 2024-08-23 22:07:48.000000000) ---
Patch Set 37:

ping reviewers.  I don't think there was anything remaining that would prevent landing, and it is the next patch with "lctl set_param -C" that would prevent non-FSNAME parameters from getting into the mount.FSNAME.params file, so that is (IMHO) not relevant for this patch.

--- Message (Timothy Day, 2024-08-27 14:53:11.000000000) ---
Patch Set 38: Code-Review+1

(1 comment)

> Patch Set 37:
> 
> > I am confused about the decision to statically link against
>  > lustre_param.c rather than just linking against liblustre itself.
>  > It doesn't seem any simpler. And from ldd, `mount.lustre` already
>  > has something like 2x as many dynamic library dependencies
>  > compared to `lctl`. What's one more?
> 
> Tim, the reason for this is a bit complex, and an artifact of how Lustre developer testing is done.  When running tests directly from the build tree (e.g. "make; cd lustre/tests; bash sanity.sh") we are still required to run the mount.lustre helper from /sbin when using "mount -t lustre ..." because that is the only place that mount will look for it (for security reasons if non-root users are able to trigger filesystem mounts).
> 
> In order for this one binary to be runnable from /sbin it is more complex to depend on a shared library that is also not installed in the system, so static linking of lustre_param.c was used to ensure mounting still worked in the various test environments (note 37 versions of this patch) and they could run "set_param" as needed.
> 
> To avoid dragging in a bunch of *other* files, a few stub functions were used to avoid dependencies for functionality that is not actually needed.  This shouldn't be needed elsewhere since most applications would link to liblustreapi.

Perhaps we could have used a link from /sbin/mount.lustre to the build tree? Is there some reason that wouldn't work?

Thanks for dropping pthreads. The stub functions are a bit ugly. But linking against pthreads and not liblustre seemed too odd.

--- Message (Andreas Dilger, 2024-08-27 15:41:37.000000000) ---
Patch Set 38:

(1 comment)

--- Message (Andreas Dilger, 2024-08-27 15:49:05.000000000) ---
Patch Set 38:

> Perhaps we could have used a link from /sbin/mount.lustre
 > to the build tree? Is there some reason that wouldn't work?

We already use a bind mount to attach lustre/utils/mount.lustre to /sbin/mount.lustre so that there is not a permanent "artifact" left in the root filesystem.  However, we can't control the runtime dynamic linking of the "mount" command, since it explicitly only runs mount helpers from /sbin and unsets environment variables like LD_LIBRARY_PATH to prevent code injection to a SUID binary.

Maybe I'll add that to the commit message...

--- Message (James Simmons, 2024-11-20 14:19:17.000000000) ---
Patch Set 42:

Its a problem for any setup that run out of the source tree (like Oleg does). Its independent of the distro. When the tests run it places mount.lustre in /sbin. Before this patch its a static binary but after this patch is becomes a libtool wrapper since liblustreapi.so is not installed but is in the source tree. You could place the real mount.lustre in /sbin but that wouldn't work since liblustreapi.so will not to be found. That is the point of the libtool wrapper. I bet the reason for place mount.lustre in /sbin is so that general mount will work. Make sense why its breaks. The whamcloud setup will work since it installs the rpms before testing.

--- Message (Andreas Dilger, 2024-11-21 21:20:44.000000000) ---
Patch Set 42:

Oleg's Gerrit Janitor testing runs out of the build tree, but doesn't have any trouble, so I blame libtool. 

I would be totally OK to move to a static liblustreapi.a linking, since we don't really need much of the library for this.  Another option would be to just link the modified .o file(s) directly into mount.lustre.

There is a separate question whether this should print the local parameters to stdout during mount, or if this will screw up other admin stuff?  It might be better to write this to syslog rather than stdout?

This even works when I'm not in the build directory:

 [root@twoshoes .../lustre/tests]# cd /
 [root@twoshoes /]# mount -t lustre mookie-gig:/myth /myth
 osc.myth-OST0000-osc-ffff9314cdb3a000.max_dirty_mb=256

 osc.myth-OST0004-osc-ffff9314cdb3a000.max_dirty_mb=256

so I'm not sure if the issue relates to the version of libtool you have installed, and/or the "never move outside the build directory" warning is finally coming true, but it definitely works when running from the build tree.  Possibly your /sbin/mount.lustre wrapper script is not being installed correctly?

I see at the end of my mount.lustre libtool wrapper:

 [root@twoshoes /]# tail /sbin/mount.lustre
   if test -f "$progdir/$program"; then
    if test "$libtool_execute_magic" != "%%%MAGIC variable%%%"; then
      # Run the actual program with our arguments.
      func_exec_program ${1+"$@"}
    fi
  else
    # The program doesn't exist.
    $ECHO "$0: error: '$progdir/$program' does not exist" 1>&2
    $ECHO "This script is just a wrapper for $program." 1>&2
    $ECHO "See the libtool documentation for more information." 1>&2
    exit 1
  fi

and the error message you got was that "error: '/sbin/.libs/mount.lustre' does not exist", which I'm not seeing. 

Running bash tracing shows that my install process for /sbin/mount.lustre also copied the "/sbin/.libs/lt-mount.lustre" binary so that this works:

 [root@twoshoes /]# bash -vx /sbin/mount.lustre mookie-gig:/myth /myth
 + thisdir=/sbin
 + program=lt-mount.lustre
 + progdir=/sbin/.libs
 + test '!' -f /sbin/.libs/lt-mount.lustre
 ++ ls -1dt /sbin/.libs/lt-mount.lustre /sbin/.libs/../lt-mount.lustre
 ++ /usr/bin/sed 1q 
 + file=/sbin/.libs/lt-mount.lustre
 + test X/sbin/.libs/lt-mount.lustre '!=' X/sbin/.libs/lt-mount.lustre
 + test -f /sbin/.libs/lt-mount.lustre
 + test '' '!=' '%%%MAGIC variable%%%'
 + func_exec_program mookie-gig:/myth /myth
 + case " $* " in   
 + func_exec_program_core mookie-gig:/myth /myth
 + test -n ''
 + exec /sbin/.libs/lt-mount.lustre mookie-gig:/myth /myth
 [root@twoshoes /]# ls -l /sbin/.libs
 total 372
 372 -rwxr-xr-x. 1 root root 379744 Nov 26 15:18 lt-mount.lustre
 [root@twoshoes /]# ldd /sbin/.libs/lt-mount.lustre 
        :
        liblustreapi.so.1 => /usr/src/lustre-head/lustre/utils/.libs/liblustreapi.so.1 (0x00007fc06c78c000)
        liblnetconfig.so.4 => /usr/src/lustre-head/lnet/utils/lnetconfig/.libs/liblnetconfig.so.4 (0x00007fc06c54c000)
        :

and this shows it is linked against the libraries in the build tree and not any installed library.

That said, while test-framework.sh is making a bind mount for /sbin/mount.lustre -> $LUSTRE/lustre/utils/mount.lustre, I don't know what process created /sbin/.libs/mount.lustre but it was definitely created today while I was running from within the test script directory.

It looks like it is the /sbin/mount.lustre script itself that is creating the /sbin/.libs directory, since I deleted it and retried the mount, with the expectation of reproducing your error, but that failed to reproduce the error.  Running it under bash debugging shows this:

 [root@twoshoes /]# rm -r /sbin/.libs
 [root@twoshoes /]# bash -vx /sbin/mount -t lustre mookie-gig:/myth /myth
 :
 + test '!' -f /sbin/.libs/lt-mount.lustre
 + file=16256-lt-mount.lustre
 + test '!' -d /sbin/.libs
 + mkdir /sbin/.libs
 :
 + ... gcc -fPIC -D_GNU_SOURCE -D_LARGEFILE64_SOURCE=1 -D_FILE_OFFSET_BITS=64 \
    -DLUSTRE_UTILS=1 -Wall -Werror -rdynamic -o /sbin/.libs/16256-lt-mount.lustre ...
 + mv -f /sbin/.libs/16256-lt-mount.lustre /sbin/.libs/lt-mount.lustre
 + test -f /sbin/.libs/lt-mount.lustre
 :
 + exec /sbin/.libs/lt-mount.lustre mookie-gig:/myth /myth

So in conclusion, it seems like either your libtool is missing this functionality, or it cannot build the lt-mount.lustre binary during the wrapper script running.

Patch Set 42:

I see the problem. /sbin/.libs never is created. This works around the issue.

diff --git a/lustre/tests/test-framework.sh b/lustre/tests/test-framework.sh
index 962e9feaf2..31a47a5258 100755
--- a/lustre/tests/test-framework.sh
+++ b/lustre/tests/test-framework.sh
@@ -1155,6 +1155,9 @@ load_modules_local() {
                                error "can't bind $mount_lustre to $sbin_mount"
                fi
        fi
+
+       [ -f /sbin/.libs ] ||
+               ln -sf $LUSTRE/utils/.libs /sbin/.libs
 }
 
 load_modules () {
@@ -1250,6 +1253,8 @@ unload_modules() {
                        rm -f $sbin_mount
        fi
 
+       [ -L /sbin/.libs ] && rm /sbin/.libs
+
        [[ $rc -eq 0 ]] && echo "modules unloaded."
 
        return $rc

So I am somewhat wonering what's up with the /sbin/.libs directory? That's a libtool stub for pre-release dynamic builds, but in my setup I am building with a static option to sidestep this issue.

Now it looks like that broke? Do we no longer support static builds starting from this change?

--- Message (Andreas Dilger, 2024-12-20 09:47:30.000000000) ---
Patch Set 44:

> So I am somewhat wonering what's up with the /sbin/.libs directory?
 > That's a libtool stub for pre-release dynamic builds, but in my
 > setup I am building with a static option to sidestep this issue.
 > 
 > Now it looks like that broke? Do we no longer support static builds
 > starting from this change?

These are all issues related to various developer-only test environments, but are not issues in production deployments.

Oleg, if you have libtool/Makefile.am options for how to link a static liblustreapi.a to mount.lustre then I would be happy to change this and remove the "/sbin/.libs" workaround.

The need to copy /sbin/.libs was seen in James' test environment and not in autotest, but it looks related to a newer libtool version.  In Janitor the testing was previously passing, but now fails because /sbin is read-only.  I think that could also be worked around, by ignoring errors returned from creating /sbin/.libs.
